**Proposition F.43** (The Sum Block Columns primitive). For any  $y \in \mathbb{R}^{N' \times d'}$  and B that divides d' there exists a (N', 1, d', N', d') – BaseConv that computes  $sum\_column\_blocks(y, B)$ .

Proof. Define

$$z \leftarrow \text{BASECONV}(y, W, \mathbf{0}^{N' \times d'}, \mathbf{0}^{N' \times d'}, \mathbf{1}^{N' \times d'})$$

where  $\mathbf{W} \in \mathbb{R}^{d' \times d'}$  is defined as:

$$\boldsymbol{W}[i,j] \equiv \begin{cases} 1 & \text{if } j \leq B \text{ and } j - B \lfloor \frac{i}{B} \rfloor \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

The output of this layer will be:

$$\begin{aligned} (\boldsymbol{y}\boldsymbol{W} + \boldsymbol{0}^{N' \times d'}) \odot (\boldsymbol{0}^{N' \times d'} * \boldsymbol{y} + \boldsymbol{1}^{N' \times d'}) &= \boldsymbol{y}\boldsymbol{W} \\ &= \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{j=0}^{\frac{d'}{B}-1} \boldsymbol{y}[:, jB+1], \dots, \sum_{j=0}^{\frac{d'}{B}-1} \boldsymbol{y}[:, jB+B-1], \underbrace{\boldsymbol{0}, \dots, \boldsymbol{0}}_{d' - \lfloor \frac{d'}{D} \rfloor \text{times}} \end{pmatrix}, \end{aligned}$$

where the last equality follows from definition of W.

**Proposition F.44** (The 1-hot primitive). For any  $y \in \mathbb{R}^{N' \times N'}$  there exists  $a(N', \lceil \log \log(N') \rceil + O(1), N', 2N' \lceil \log N' \rceil, N') - BaseConv that computes one_hot_encoding(<math>y$ ).

*Proof.* We first give a sketch of the proof. Each row has a binary representation of a number which we want to convert to it's 1-hot encoding. In order to do this, we need to know which position in the 1-hot encoded vector needs to be 1. We need to extract information from each bit, which details which subset of positions the 1-hot encoded vector could potentially have as 1. Concretely, if the least significant bit is 0, only the even position can be represented, if that same bit is 1, only the odd positions can be represented. This pattern continues for all bits in the binary number. Each bit in the binary representation gets its own row. Finally, we take the bit wise ANDs of each row of the same binary representation to get the resulting 1-hot encoded vector. Next, we present the details.

First compute  $z_1 \in \mathbb{R}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}$  defined as:

$$z_1 \leftarrow \text{repeat\_matrix}(\boldsymbol{y}, 2\lceil \log(N') \rceil).$$

Define

$$z_2 \leftarrow \text{BaseConv}(z_1, I^{N' \times N'}, \mathbf{0}^{2N' \lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}, \mathbf{0}^{2N' \lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}, b_2^2),$$

where  $b_2 \in \mathbb{R}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}$  is defined as for  $1 \le i \le 2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil$  and  $1 \le j \le N'$ :

$$\boldsymbol{b}_2^2[i,j] \equiv \begin{cases} 1 & \text{if } \left( \left\lfloor \frac{i}{N'} \right\rfloor \mod \lceil \log(N') \rceil \right) + 1 = j \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

Note that  $z_1$  has  $2 \log(N')$  copies of the binary representations in the first column block. When we zero them out to get  $z_2$ , the  $(i \mod \log(N'))$ th matrix stores the value of the ith bit with all others being set to zero. Compute  $z_3 \in \mathbb{R}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}$  by storing the sum all columns in the first column. Being that each row only has a single

non-zero entry, this is equivalent to moving every one of these non-zero entries to the first column. Define

$$z_3 \leftarrow \text{sum\_all\_columns}(z_2).$$

Compute  $z_4 \in \mathbb{R}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}$  by copying the first column to all other columns. Define

$$z_4 \leftarrow \text{repeat\_columns}(z_3, N').$$

Then, we will take a Hadamard product of  $z_4$  with a binary representation matrix. Define

$$z_5 \leftarrow \texttt{BaseConv}(z_4, \mathbf{0}^{N' \times N'}, b_1^5, 1, \mathbf{0}^{2N' \lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'})$$
.

In the above,  $b_1^5$  has the positions where a binary number with that has that bit set to a 1 could fall(and 0 if it in the bottom half of the matrix. We will define it in blocks where  $1 \le i \le 2\lceil \log N' \rceil$ ,  $1 \le k \le N'$ ,  $1 \le j \le N'$ 

$$\boldsymbol{b}_1^5[(i,k),j] \equiv \begin{cases} 1 & \text{if } j \mod 2^i \geq 2^{i-1} \text{ and } i \leq \lceil \log N' \rceil \\ 1 & \text{if } j \mod 2^i < 2^{i-1} \text{ and } i > \lceil \log N' \rceil \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

Next, we will combine the two representations:

$$\bm{z}_6 \leftarrow \texttt{BaseConv}\left(\bm{z}_5, \bm{0}^{N' \times N'}, \bm{b}_1^6, \bm{h}^6, \bm{0}^{2N' \lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}\right),$$

where  $b_1^6$ ,  $h^6$  are defined as:

$$\bm{b}_1^6 = \begin{pmatrix} \bm{0}^{(N'\lceil \log N' \rceil) \times N'} \ \bm{1}^{(N'\lceil \log N' \rceil) \times N'} \end{pmatrix}, \bm{h}^6 = \begin{pmatrix} \bm{e}_1^{(N'\lceil \log N' \rceil)} \ \bm{e}_1^{(N'\lceil \log N' \rceil)} \end{pmatrix}.$$

We now specify the results of this kernel:

$$\begin{split} \left( \boldsymbol{h}^6 * \boldsymbol{z_5} \right) &= \operatorname{coeff} \left( \left( 1 + \boldsymbol{X}^{N'\lceil \log N' \rceil} \right) \cdot \boldsymbol{z_5}(\boldsymbol{x}) \right) \\ &= \operatorname{coeff} \left( \boldsymbol{z_5}(\boldsymbol{x}) + \boldsymbol{z_5}(\boldsymbol{x}) \cdot \boldsymbol{X}^{N'\lceil \log N' \rceil} \right) \\ &= \boldsymbol{z_5} + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{z_5}, \boldsymbol{X}^{N'\lceil \log N' \rceil}) \end{split}$$

By combining the possible positions based on a 0 or 1 being present in the binary number,  $z_6$  now stores the expanded binary representation in each row block in the bottom half of the matrix. We move this to the top half as shown below:

$$z_7 \leftarrow \text{shift-up}(z_6, N' \lceil \log N' \rceil).$$

Finally we do a bit wise multiplication between corresponding rows. For  $0 \le m < \lceil \log \log N' \rceil$  such that on the m'th iteration the following function is performed:

$$\begin{aligned} \boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}' \leftarrow \text{BASECONV}(\boldsymbol{z}_{8,m-1}, \boldsymbol{I}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}, \boldsymbol{0}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}, \boldsymbol{h}_m, \boldsymbol{0}^{2N'\lceil \log N' \rceil \times N'}) \\ \boldsymbol{z}_{8,m} \leftarrow \text{shift-up}(\boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}', N'2^m) \end{aligned}$$

Where  $z_{8,-1} \equiv z_7$  and  $h_m$  is defined below:

$$\bm{h}_m = \begin{pmatrix} \bm{e}_1^{(2^m)} \ \bm{e}_1^{(2^m-2N'\lceil\log N'\rceil)} \end{pmatrix}.$$

The computation of this convolution will result in:

$$(\boldsymbol{h}_m * \boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}) = \operatorname{coeff}\left(\left(1 + X^{(2^m)}\right) \cdot \boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}\right)(x)$$

$$= \operatorname{coeff}\left(\boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}(x) + \boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}(x) \cdot X^{(2^m)}\right)$$

$$= \boldsymbol{z}_{8,m} + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{z}_{8,m}, X^{(2^m)})$$

 $z_7$  holds the possible positions of of the "1" in the one hot vector for each bit in the binary representation. This step takes a bit-wise and of the rows corresponding to the same binary representation so that we are left with the 1-hot encoding of the original binary representation. The idea is that for each bit in each binary representation of each value, there is a row in  $z_7$  that represents the possible positions, in the form of a bitmap, that this binary number can encode. When we bitwise AND all of these rows together, we are left with the position that satisfies all the constraints and is therefore the index that these binary numbers encoded.

<span id="page-56-0"></span>**Proposition F.45** (The Remembering Primitive). For any  $x \in \mathbb{R}^{n \times d'}$ ,  $v_1 \in \mathbb{R}^{r \times d'}$ ,  $v_2 \in \mathbb{R}^{m-r}$  where n = t - r contained in some  $y \in \mathbb{R}^{N' \times d'}$  such that  $v_1$  is in the first r rows, x is in the next n rows, 0s fill up the next s rows, and  $v_2$  are in the next m - r rows, for some  $3n + 3m + 2s + 2t \le N'$  so that for  $h \in \mathbb{R}^{n \times d}$  and  $\mathbf{W} \in \mathbb{R}^{d' \times d'}$  with  $x * h \in \mathbb{R}^{(n+s) \times d'}$  and  $v * h \in \mathbb{R}^{(m+t) \times d'}$ , where  $v \in \mathbb{R}^{m \times d}$  is defined as  $v_2 + \text{shift\_down}(v_1, m - r)$ , there exists a (N', 8, d', N', d') - BaseConv that computes  $v \in \mathbb{R}^{m \times d'}$ , where  $v \in \mathbb{R}^{m \times d'}$  and  $v \in \mathbb{R}^{m \times d'}$  as defined below:

$$f(\boldsymbol{u}) = \left( \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{u} \boldsymbol{W} \\ \boldsymbol{0}^{s \times d'} \end{pmatrix} + \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{b}_1 \\ \boldsymbol{1}^{s \times d'} \end{pmatrix} \right) \odot \left( \boldsymbol{u} * \boldsymbol{h} + \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{b}_2 \\ \boldsymbol{0}^{s \times d'} \end{pmatrix} \right)$$

*Proof.* First, we will convert the y so that it stores v in consecutive rows to get  $z_1$ . Recall

$$\begin{aligned} \begin{aligned} \begin{aligned} & \leftarrow \boldsymbol{v}_1 \rightarrow \ & \leftarrow \boldsymbol{x} \rightarrow \ & \boldsymbol{o}^{s \times d'} \ & \leftarrow \boldsymbol{v}_2 \rightarrow \ & \boldsymbol{o}^{(N'-m-s-n) \times d'} \end{aligned} .$$

We compute  $z_1$  as:

$$\boldsymbol{z}_1 \leftarrow \text{BaseConv}(\boldsymbol{y}, \boldsymbol{0}^{d' \times d'}, \boldsymbol{b}_1^1, \boldsymbol{h}^1, \boldsymbol{0}^{N' \times d'}),$$

where the kernels h <sup>1</sup> ∈ R N′×d and b 1 <sup>1</sup> ∈ R N′×d are given by:

$$\begin{aligned} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} .

We now specify the result of this kernel:

$$\begin{split} \left(\boldsymbol{h}^1 * \boldsymbol{y}\right) &= \operatorname{coeff}\left((1 + X^{n+s+m}) \cdot \left(\boldsymbol{v}_1(X) + \boldsymbol{x}(X) \cdot X^r + \boldsymbol{v}_2(X) \cdot X^{n+s+r}\right)\right) \\ &= \operatorname{coeff}\left(\boldsymbol{v}_1(X) + \boldsymbol{x}(X) \cdot X^r + \boldsymbol{v}_2 \cdot X^{n+s+r} + \boldsymbol{v}_1(X) \cdot X^{n+s+m} + \boldsymbol{x}(X) \cdot X^{n+s+m+r} + \boldsymbol{v}_2 \cdot X^{2n+2s+m+r}\right) \\ &= \boldsymbol{v}_1 + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{x},r) + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{v}_2,n+s+r) + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{v}_1,n+s+m) \\ &+ \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{x},n+s+m+r) + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{v}_2,2n+2s+m+r). \end{split}$$

With this we have:

$$\begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} Next compute z<sup>2</sup> :

$$z_2 \leftarrow \text{shift-up}(z_1, r),$$

as seen in (Arora et al., 2023a) Proposition F.38.

At this point  $z_2$  looks like:

$$\begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{x} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{s\times d'} \ \boldsymbol{v} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{n\times d'} \ \boldsymbol{\vdots} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{n\times d'} \end{pmatrix}$$

Next, we will apply f to  $z_2$  to get f(x) but also retain a unchanged version of v. Define

$$z_3 \leftarrow \mathsf{BASECONV}(z_2, W, b_1^3, h^3, b_2^3),$$

with the kernels  $h^3$ ,  $b_1^3$ , and  $b_2^3$  for this layer are given by:

$$\begin{aligned} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{aligned} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} Remember that  $W, h, b_1, b_2$  come from the definition of f. We specify the result of this kernel as:

$$\begin{split} \left( \boldsymbol{h}^3 * \boldsymbol{z}_2 \right) &= \operatorname{coeff} \left( \left( \boldsymbol{h}(X) + X^{n+s+m+t} \right) \cdot \left( \boldsymbol{x}(X) + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{n+s} \right) \right) \\ &= \operatorname{coeff} \left( \boldsymbol{h} \cdot \boldsymbol{x}(X) + \boldsymbol{h} \cdot \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{n+s} + \boldsymbol{x}(X) \cdot X^{n+s+m+t} + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{2n+2s+m+t} \right) \\ &= \boldsymbol{h} * \boldsymbol{x} + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{h} * \boldsymbol{v}, n+s) \\ &+ \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{x}, n+s+m+t) + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{v}, 2n+2s+m+t). \end{split}$$

With this we have

Note that  $\begin{pmatrix} xW \\ 0^{s\times d'} \end{pmatrix} + \begin{pmatrix} b_1 \\ 0^{s\times d'} \end{pmatrix} \odot \begin{pmatrix} h*x + \begin{pmatrix} b_2 \\ 0^{s\times d'} \end{pmatrix} \end{pmatrix}$  is f(x) as defined. This next step will mask out duplicate and unnecessary x and v values. Define

$$\boldsymbol{z}_4 \leftarrow \text{BaseConv}(\boldsymbol{z}_3, \boldsymbol{I}^{N' \times d'}, \boldsymbol{0}^{N' \times d'}, \boldsymbol{0}^{N' \times d'}, \boldsymbol{b}_2^4),$$

where the kernel  $\pmb{b}_2^4 \in \mathbb{R}^{N' \times d'}$  for this layer is given by:

$$\boldsymbol{b_2^4} \leftarrow \begin{bmatrix} \boldsymbol{1}^{(n+s)\times d'} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{(m+t)\times d'} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{(n+s)\times d'} \ \boldsymbol{1}^{(m)\times d'} \end{pmatrix}.$$

We will specify the output of this layer:

$$\boldsymbol{z}_4 = \boldsymbol{z}_3 \odot \boldsymbol{b}_2^4 = \begin{pmatrix} f(\boldsymbol{x}) & f(\boldsymbol{x}) & \boldsymbol{0} & \boldsymbol{1} & \boldsymbol{1} & \boldsymbol{1} & $$\boldsymbol{z}_5 \leftarrow \text{BASECONV}(\boldsymbol{z}_4, \boldsymbol{0}^{d' \times d'}, \boldsymbol{b}_1^5, \boldsymbol{h}^5, \boldsymbol{0}^{N' \times d'}),$$

$$\begin{split} \left(\boldsymbol{h}^5 * \boldsymbol{z}_4\right) &= \operatorname{coeff}\left((1 + X^{n+s+m+t}) \cdot \left(f(\boldsymbol{x})(X) + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{2n+2s+m+t}\right)\right) \\ &= \operatorname{coeff}\left(f(\boldsymbol{x})(X) + f(\boldsymbol{x})(X) \cdot X^{n+s+m+t} + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{2n+2s+m+t} + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{3n+3s+2m+2t}\right) \\ &= f(\boldsymbol{x}) + \operatorname{shift-down}(f(\boldsymbol{x}), n+s+m+t) + \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{v}, 2n+2s+m+t) \\ &+ \operatorname{shift-down}(\boldsymbol{v}, 3n+3s+2m+2t). \end{split}$$

Specifically the convolution does this:

$$\begin{split} \left( \boldsymbol{h}^6 * \boldsymbol{z}_5 \right) &= \operatorname{coeff} \left( (1 + X^{2n + 2s + 2m + t}) \cdot \left( ((f(\boldsymbol{x}))(X)) \cdot X^{n + m + s + t} + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{2n + m + 2s + t} \right) \right) \\ &= \operatorname{coeff} \left( (f(\boldsymbol{x}))(X) \right) \cdot X^{n + m + s + t} + \operatorname{coeff} \left( (f(\boldsymbol{x})(X)) \cdot X^{3n + 3m + 3s + 2t} \right) \\ &+ \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{2n + 1m + 2s + t} + \boldsymbol{v}(X) \cdot X^{4n + 3m + 4s + 2t} \\ &= \operatorname{shift-down} ((f(\boldsymbol{x})(X)), n + m + s + t) \\ &+ \operatorname{shift-down} ((f(\boldsymbol{x})(X)), 3n + 3m + 3s + 2t) \\ &+ \operatorname{shift-down} (\boldsymbol{v}, 2n + m + 2s + t) + \operatorname{shift-down} (\boldsymbol{v}, 4n + 3m + 4s + 2t). \end{split}$$

$$\begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} \begin{align*} Finally we get,

$$z_7 \leftarrow \text{shift-up}(z_6, 2n + 2m + 2s + t - r)$$

The final output of this layer is:

$$\begin{aligned} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \egn{pmatrix} \egn{pmatrix} \egn{pmatrix} \egn{pmatrix} \e$$

which is our final output.

<span id="page-62-0"></span>**Corollary F.46.** Let  ${\bf y}$  be as in Proposition F.45 but now let f be implemented with  ${\tt BaseConv}(N',L,d',N',d')$ . Then  ${\tt remember}({\bf y},r,t,f)$  where t-r=n can be implemented with  ${\tt BaseConv}(N',O(L),d',N',d')$ .

*Proof.* The Remember primitive can be used to implement any number of BaseConv layers. As shown, the remember primitive can perform a BaseConv operation on a portion of a matrix while maintaining the values of the rest. This output matrix can then be fed through another remember primitive repeatedly such that any number of BaseConv layers can be performed through remember.

**Definition F.47.** Being that primitives 1-7 can be implemented using BaseConv layers and that remember can apply BaseConv to a continuous subsection of a matrix, we can implement these primitives on subsections of any matrix "through" remember. This will be represented as Remember (i, j, f) where i and j are the start and end rows that will be effected, respectively, and f is the function which will be applied to them.

#### F.6.2. PROOF OF THEOREM F.30

We first mathematically state the major steps, after which we will show how to implement each step using BaseConv layers.

1. Input: Q, K, V.

OUTPUT: Q, K', V where  $K' \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$  is defined below.

In steps 1.1 and 1.2, for  $1 \le i \le N$ , replace each 1 in K[i,:] by  $bin(i)^{\top}$  to get  $\overline{K} \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$ . Then in step 1.3 then we compute K' where every row is the sum of all previous rows and itself in  $\overline{K}$ .

1.1 INPUT: Q, K, V.

OUTPUT:  $Q, \overline{K}', V$  where  $\overline{K}' \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$  is defined below.

$$\overline{\bm{K}}' := \texttt{repeat\_columns}(\bm{K}, b).$$

1.2 Input:  $\boldsymbol{Q}, \overline{\boldsymbol{K}}', \boldsymbol{V}.$ 

OUTPUT:  $Q, \overline{K}, V$  where  $\mathbf{B} \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}, \overline{K}' \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$  are defined below.

<span id="page-63-0"></span>
$$\mathbf{B}[i, jb + 1 : (j+1)b] := \operatorname{bin}(i)^{\top} \text{ for all } 1 \le i \le N \text{ and } 1 \le j \le d.$$

$$\overline{K} := \mathbf{B} \odot \overline{K}'.$$
(37)

1.3 Input:  $Q, \overline{K}, V$ .

OUTPUT: Q, K', V where  $K' \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$  is defined below.

$$\bm{K}'[i,:] := \sum_{i=1}^{i} \overline{\bm{K}}[j,:] \text{ for all } 1 \leq i \leq N.$$

2. Input: Q, K', V.

OUTPUT:  $\overline{M}$ , V where  $\overline{M} \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$  is defined as follows.

In steps 2.1-2.3, compute  $\overline{\boldsymbol{M}}[i,:]$  so that  $\overline{\boldsymbol{M}}[i,1:b] = \mathrm{bin}(j)^{\top}$  where  $\boldsymbol{Q}[i,:] = \boldsymbol{K}[j,:]$  for every  $1 \leq i \leq N$ . Note that by assumption (ii) only one such j exists.

2.1 INPUT: Q, K', V.

OUTPUT: Q', K', V.

Compute  $Q' \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times db}$  to be Q with each column repeated b times.

$$Q' = \text{repeat\_columns}(Q, b).$$

2.2 Input: Q', K', V.

OUTPUT:  $\overline{\bm{M}}', \bm{V}$ .

Compute  $\overline{M}'$  as it is defined below:

$$\overline{M}' = Q' \odot K'$$
.

Some column block of  $\overline{M}'$  holds bin(j) such that Q[i,:] matches K[j,:], we now move it to the first column block in step 2.3.

2.3 INPUT:  $\overline{M}'$ , V.

OUTPUT:  $\overline{M}$ , V. Compute  $\overline{M}$  as it is defined below:

$$\overline{\boldsymbol{M}} = \texttt{sum\_column\_blocks}(\overline{\boldsymbol{M}}', b).$$

The first b entries in the i'th row  $\overline{M}$  holds  $\mathrm{bin}(j)$  such that  $\boldsymbol{Q}[i,:]$  matches  $\boldsymbol{K}[j,:]$ .

3. Input:  $\overline{M}$ , V.

OUTPUT: L, V where  $L \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times N}$ .

Compute L from  $\overline{M}$  as defined below:

$$L = C \odot (QK^{\top}).$$

Compute  $L \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times N}$  from  $\overline{M}$  such that the binary representation of j in the i'th block is converted into 1-hot encoding of j in the i'th row of  $\overline{M}$ . Define

$$L \leftarrow \texttt{one\_hot\_encoding}(\overline{M})$$

So we now have computed  $L = C \odot (QK^\top)$ . All that's left to do is to compute  $L \times V$ . While mathematically this is a simple operation, we will implement this in multiple steps so that it is easy to implement this with BaseConv layers on input  $\binom{L}{V}$ .

4. INPUT: L, V.

OUTPUT:  $L, \overline{V}$ , where  $\overline{V} \in \mathbb{R}^{N\overline{b} \times d}$  is defined below.

In steps 4.1 and 4.2, compute  $\overline{V}$  from V where the v'th column holds the information for  $bin(v) \in \{0,1\}^{\overline{b}}$ , for every  $1 \le v \le d$ :

4.1 INPUT: L, V.

OUTPUT:  $L, \overline{V}_1$ , where  $\overline{V}_1 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\overline{b} \times d}$  is defined below.

$$\overline{\bm{V}}_1 := \texttt{repeat\_matrix}(\bm{V}, \overline{b}).$$

4.2 INPUT:  $L, \overline{V}_1$ .

OUTPUT:  $L, \overline{V}$ , where  $\overline{V}_1 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\overline{b} \times d}$  is defined below. First, define  $\mathbf{B}' \in \mathbb{N}^{N\overline{b} \times d}$  for  $1 \leq i \leq \overline{b}, 1 \leq k \leq N, 1 \leq j \leq d$  as:

<span id="page-64-0"></span>
$$\mathbf{B}'[(i,k),j] \equiv \begin{cases} 1 & \text{if } j \mod 2^i \ge 2^{i-1} \\ 0 & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$
 (38)

Then

$$\overline{\boldsymbol{V}} := \overline{\boldsymbol{V}}_1 \odot \mathbf{B}'.$$

5. Input:  $L, \overline{V}$ .

OUTPUT: L, V', where  $V' \in \mathbb{R}^{N\overline{b} \times d}$  is defined below.

Compute V' from  $\overline{V}$  such that all the non-zero encodings of columns of  $\overline{V}$  are moved to 1st column and the other columns are zeroed out, specifically for  $1 \le i \le Nb$ :

$$\bm{V}'[:,i] := \begin{cases} \sum_{j=1}^d \overline{\bm{V}}[:,j] & \text{if } i=1 \\ \bm{0}^{N\bar{b}} & \text{otherwise}. \end{cases}$$

The summation of each column of  $\overline{V}$  performs this desired move action because each row of  $\overline{V}$  has at most 1 non zero value as each row of B' is a 1-hot encoding.

6. Input: L, V'.

OUTPUT:  $L, V_1$  where  $V_1 \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times N\bar{b}}$  is defined below.

Compute  $V_1$  from V' in steps 6.1-6.6 such that for  $1 \le k \le N$  and  $W \in \mathbb{R}^{N\overline{b} \times N\overline{b}}$ :

$$\boldsymbol{W}[i,j] = \begin{cases} 1 & \text{if } i = \left(\left((j-1)N + \left\lfloor \frac{i-1}{N} \right\rfloor\right) \mod N\overline{b}\right) + 1 \\ 0 & \text{otherwise}. \end{cases}$$

$$V_1[k,:] := (V'[:,1]^\top)W.$$

W is a permutation matrix which reorders the values such that values relating to the same index rather than values relating to the same copy of the matrix, made in step 4.1, are adjacent.

6.1 INPUT: L, V'.

OHTPHT:  $L V_2$ 

Compute  $V_2 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\overline{b} \times N\overline{b}}$  from V' where  $V_2$  has the 1st column of V' repeated  $N\overline{b}$  times, as defined below for  $1 < i < N\overline{b}$ :

$$V_2[:, j] = V'[:, 1]$$

6.2 INPUT:  $L, V_2$ .

OUTPUT:  $L, V_3$ .

Compute  $V_3 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\bar{b} \times N\bar{b}}$  from  $V_2$  by zeroing out all but the diagonal:

$$V_3 = I^{Nb \times Nb} \odot V_2.$$

6.3 INPUT:  $L, V_3$ .

OUTPUT:  $L, V_4$ .

Compute  $V_4 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\bar{b}\times N\bar{b}}$  from  $V_3$  and W such that the values are permuted such that the values grouped by which row they represent, rather than the matrix repeat number they were in. Where  $V_4$  is defined as:

$$V_4 = V_3 W$$
.

6.4 INPUT:  $L, V_4$ .

OUTPUT:  $L, V_5$ .

Compute  $V_5 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\bar{b}\times N\bar{b}}$  from  $V_4$  such that  $V_5[1,:]$  is the sum of all rows by making  $V_5[N\bar{b},:]$  the sum of all rows of  $V_4$  followed by zeroing the rest of rows. I.e. for all  $1 \le i, j \le N\bar{b}$ :

$$\bm{V}_5[i,:] := \begin{cases} \sum_{k=1}^{N\overline{b}} \bm{V}_4[k,:] & \text{if } i = N\overline{b} \ \bm{0} & \text{otherwise}. \end{cases}$$

6.5 INPUT:  $L, V_5$ .

OUTPUT:  $L, V_6$ .

Compute  $V_6 \in \mathbb{R}^{N\bar{b}\times N\bar{b}}$  from  $V_5$  such that  $V_6[1,:] = V_5[N\bar{b},:]$  and the rest of the rows be zeroed out. I.e. for all  $1 \le i, j \le N\bar{b}$ :

$$\boldsymbol{V}_6[i,:] := \begin{cases} \boldsymbol{V}_5[N\bar{b},:] & \text{if } i=1 \ \boldsymbol{0} & \text{otherwise}. \end{cases}$$

6.6 INPUT:  $L, V_6$ .

OUTPUT:  $L, V_1$ .

Compute  $V_1$  from  $V_6$  by copying  $V_6[1,:]$  to rest of the rows.

$$V_1[i,:] := V_6[1,:]$$
 for all  $1 \le i \le N$ .

At this point, each row of  $V_1$  now has the same values as the first column of V' permuted in the way that was stated in 6.3.

7. INPUT:  $L, V_1$ .

OUTPUT:  $\overline{L}$  where  $\overline{L} \in R^{N \times Nb}$  is defined below.

Compute  $\overline{L}$  such that the single 1 in L[i,:] (say at position  $0 \le j < N$ ) is replaced by  $bin(j)^{\top}$ . In other words, the i'th query were to match a key in position j, if the i'th row of  $\overline{L}$  would have a representation of the matching value at the j'th block.

7.1 INPUT:  $L, V_1$ .

OUTPUT: L'.  $V_1$ 

Compute  $L' \in R^{N \times N\overline{b}}$  by repeating each column of  $L\overline{b}$  times:

$$L'[:,j] = L\left[:, \left\lceil \frac{j}{\overline{b}} \right\rceil \right] \text{ if } 1 \le j \le N\overline{b}.$$

7.2 Input:  $L', V_1$ .

OUTPUT:  $\overline{\bm{L}}$ 

Compute  $\overline{L} \leftarrow L' \odot V_1$ .

8. Input:  $\overline{\boldsymbol{L}}$ .

OUTPUT:  $\overline{L}_1 = L \times V$ , the final output.

8.1 Input:  $\overline{\boldsymbol{L}}$ .

OUTPUT:  $\overline{L}_2 \in \mathbb{R}^{N \times (N \times \overline{b})}$  by summing up  $\overline{b}$  chunks of columns of  $\overline{L}$  and store the result in 1st block column and zero out remaining columns to get  $\overline{L}_2$ , specifically for  $1 \le j \le \overline{b}$ :

$$\overline{L}_2[:,(i,j)] \equiv \begin{cases} \sum_{k=1}^{N} L[:,(k,j)] & \text{if } i = 1\\ \mathbf{0}^{N \times \overline{b}} & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

8.2 Input:  $\overline{\boldsymbol{L}}_2$ 

OUTPUT:  $\overline{L}_1$  by replacing the binary representation in 1st block column by corresponding 1-hot encoding. Compute  $\overline{L}_1$  from  $\overline{L}_2$  such that for  $1 \le i \le N$ ,  $\overline{L}_1[i,:] = e_\ell^{(d)}$  where  $\overline{L}_2[i,(1,:)] = \text{bin}(\ell)^\top$ .

Next, using the primitives defined in Appendix F.6.1, we show how each step above would be implemented with BASECONV layers. Instead of 3 separate matrices as shown in the math layout, we will have a single matrix,  $\mathbf{Y} \in \mathbb{R}^{3N \times d}$  which contains the information of all three.

$$\mathbf{Y} = \begin{pmatrix} Q \ K \ V \end{pmatrix}.$$

The internal dimension will be  $(4\overline{N}\log(\overline{N}), \overline{N}\log(\overline{N}))$ . For notational convenience, we define

$$z = \overline{N} \log(\overline{N}).$$

Specifically, the input  $\pmb{Y} \in \mathbb{R}^{3z \times d}$  has the top left matrix of  $3N \times d$  holding  $\begin{pmatrix} \pmb{Q} \\ \pmb{K} \\ \pmb{V} \end{pmatrix}$ .

Define

$$\mathbf{Y}_0 \leftarrow \text{BASECONV}(\mathbf{Y}, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}, \boldsymbol{b}_1^0, \boldsymbol{h}_0, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}),$$

where  $\boldsymbol{b}_1^0 \in \mathbb{R}^{4z \times z}$  and  $\boldsymbol{h}_0 \in \mathbb{R}^{4z \times z}$  are defined as:

$$\begin{aligned} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} egi$$

The vectors that make up the convolution have dimension z - N because K and V are not top left justified in the original matrix. This produces a matrix where Q, K and V all sit in the top left position in their own sub-matrix surrounded by

zeros. The structure is:

$$\mathbf{Y}_0 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{Q}^p \ \boldsymbol{K}^p \ \boldsymbol{V}^p \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

where

$$\boldsymbol{Q}^p = \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{Q}, \boldsymbol{0}^{N \times (z)} \\ \boldsymbol{0}^{(z-N) \times (z)} \end{pmatrix}, \boldsymbol{K}^p = \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{K}, \boldsymbol{0}^{N \times (z)} \\ \boldsymbol{0}^{(z-N) \times (z)} \end{pmatrix}, \boldsymbol{V}^p = \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{V}, \boldsymbol{0}^{N \times (z)} \\ \boldsymbol{0}^{(z-N) \times (z)} \end{pmatrix}.$$

- 1. Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_1$  in steps 1.1-1.2.
  - 1.1 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_1' \leftarrow \texttt{remember}\left(\mathbf{Y}_0, z+1, 2z, f_1\right)$  where  $f_1$  is defined as:

repeat-columns(
$$\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_0, b$$
).

This results in

$$\mathbf{Y}_1' \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{Q}^p \ \hline \boldsymbol{\overline{K}}' \ \hline \boldsymbol{V}^p \ \hline \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This repeats the columns of  ${\pmb K}$   $\overline{b}$  times and doesn't change  $\overline{{\pmb Q}}$  or  $\overline{{\pmb V}}$  with BaseConv(4z,O(1),z,4z,z) via Corollary F.46.

1.2 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_1'' \leftarrow \text{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_1', z+1, 2z, f_1')$  where  $f_1'$  is defined as:

BaseConv(
$$\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_{1}', \mathbf{I}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{B}$$
).

Where **B** is defined as it was in equation 37. This results in

$$\mathbf{Y}_1'' \equiv \begin{array}{c} \begin{array}{c} Q^p \ \hline \overline{K} \ \hline V^p \ \hline \begin{array}{c} 0^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This replaces each 1 in  $\boldsymbol{K}$  with the binary representation of the row with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Proposition F.45.

1.3 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_1 \leftarrow \text{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_1'', z+1, 2z, f_1'')$  where  $f_1''$  is defined as:

$$\texttt{cumulative\_sum}(\overline{\overline{\mathbf{Y}}}_1'').$$

This results in

$$\mathbf{Y}_1 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{Q}^p \ \boldsymbol{K}' \ \boldsymbol{V}^p \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

- 2. Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_2$  in steps 2.1-2.3.
  - 2.1 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_2' \leftarrow \text{Remember}(\mathbf{Y}_1, 1, z, f_2)$  where  $f_2$  is defined as:

repeat-columns 
$$(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_1,b)$$
 .

This results in

$$\mathbf{Y}_2' \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{Q'} \ \boldsymbol{K'} \ \boldsymbol{V}^p \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This repeats the columns of  ${\bm Q}$   ${\bar b}$  times with BaseConv(4z,O(1),z,4z,z) via Corollary F.46.

2.2 Compute  $Y_2$  as the Hadamard product of the first and second position stored in the second position. This can be done with the following substeps:

$$\mathbf{Y}_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{BASECONV}(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_2', \boldsymbol{I}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}, \boldsymbol{h}^2, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}).$$

Where  $h^2 \in \mathbb{R}^{4z \times z}$  is defined as:

$$\bm{h}^2 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \bm{0}^{z \times z} \ e_1^{(z)} \ \bm{0}^{z \times z} \ \bm{0}^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This layer computes:

$$\mathbf{Y}_2'' = \mathbf{Y}_2' \odot \left( \boldsymbol{h}^2 * \mathbf{Y}_2' \right) = \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{Q'} \ \boldsymbol{K'} \ \boldsymbol{V} \ \boldsymbol{1}^z \end{pmatrix} \odot \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{0}^{z \times z} \ \boldsymbol{Q'} \ \boldsymbol{Q'} \ \boldsymbol{K'} \ \boldsymbol{K'} \ \boldsymbol{V} \end{pmatrix} \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{0}^{z \times z} \ \boldsymbol{Q'} \odot \boldsymbol{K'} \ \boldsymbol{K'} \ \boldsymbol{V} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Next, we mask out the unnecessary position using

$$\mathbf{Y}_2^3 \equiv \mathsf{BASECONV}(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_2'', \boldsymbol{b}_1^2, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}, \boldsymbol{e}_1^{4z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}).$$

Where  $b_1^2 \in \mathbb{R}^{4z \times z}$  is defined as:

$$\bm{b}_1^2 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \bm{0}^{z \times z} \ \bm{1}^{z \times z} \ \bm{0}^{z \times z} \ \bm{1}^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This layer computes:

$$\mathbf{Y}_2^3 = \boldsymbol{b}_1^2 \odot \mathbf{Y}_2'' = \begin{pmatrix} \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{1}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \mathbf{0}^{z im$$

Finally, we shift up:

$$\mathbf{Y}_2^4 \leftarrow \text{shift-up}(\mathbf{Y}_2^3, z)$$
.

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_2^4 = \begin{pmatrix} \overline{\bm{M}}' \ \bm{0}^{z\times z} \ \hline \bm{V} \ \bm{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This was done using BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via the vanilla BaseConv layers and Proposition F.38.

2.3 Sum up block columns in the first position to move the binary representations to the first column blocks through remember  $(\mathbf{Y}_2^4, 1, z, f_2)$ . Where  $f_2$  is defined as:

$$\verb"sum_column_blocks"(\overline{\overline{\mathbf{Y}}}_2^4,b).$$

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_2 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \overline{M} \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \ \hline V \ \mathbf{0}^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Through this step, we have computed  $\overline{\boldsymbol{M}}$  with BaseConv(4z,O(1),z,4z,z) via Corollary F.46..

3. Compute  $Y_3 \leftarrow \text{Remember}(Y_2, 1, z, f_3)$  where  $f_3$  is defined by:

one\_hot\_encoding(
$$\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_2$$
)

This step was computed with BaseConv $(4z, O(\lceil \log \log \overline{N} \rceil, z, 4z, z)$  via Corollary F.46. This converts  $\overline{M}$  to be 1-hot encoded in  $O(\overline{N} \log \overline{N})$  BaseConv layers. This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_3 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{L} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z \times z} \ \boldsymbol{V} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

We move this binary representation to the first column block with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Proposition F.38.

4. Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_4$  in steps 4.1 and 4.2.

4.1 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_4' \leftarrow \texttt{remember}\left(\mathbf{Y}_3, 2z+1, 3z, f_4'\right)$  where  $f_4'$  is defined as:

repeat-matrix 
$$(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_3, \overline{b})$$

This results in:

$$\begin{pmatrix} L \ \hline 0^{z \times z} \ \hline \hline V' \ \hline 0^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

We repeat V matrix  $\bar{b}$  times with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Corollary F.46.

4.2 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_4 \leftarrow \text{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_4', 2z+1, 3z, f_4)$  where  $f_4$  is defined as:

BaseConv (
$$\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_4', \boldsymbol{I}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{B}'$$
).

Where  $\mathbf{B}'$  is defined as it was in equation 38.

This results in:

$$\begin{pmatrix} L \ 0^{z \times z} \ \hline \overline{V} \ 0^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This step can be done with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Proposition F.45.

5. Compute  $Y_5 \leftarrow \text{remember}(Y_4, 2z + 1, 3z, f_5)$  )where  $f_5$  is defined as:

$$\verb"sum-all-columns" (\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_4)$$

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_5 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} L \ \mathbf{0}^{z\times z} \ V' \ \mathbf{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Now each row of V' has that one moved to the first column if it existed with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Corollary F.46.

6. Compute  $Y_6$  through in steps 6.1-6.6.

6.1 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_6' \leftarrow \texttt{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_5, 2z+1, 3z, f_6')$  where  $f_6'$  is defined as:

repeat\_columns 
$$(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_5, N \overline{b})$$
 .

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_6' \equiv \begin{pmatrix} L \ \mathbf{0}^{z\times z} \ \hline V_2 \ \mathbf{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here we repeat the columns of V' with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Corollary F.46.

6.2 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_6'' \leftarrow \text{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_6', 2z+1, 3z, f_6'')$  where  $f_6''$  is defined as:

BaseConv (
$$\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_{6}^{\prime},\mathbf{0},\boldsymbol{I}^{z\times z},\boldsymbol{e}_{1}^{(z)},\boldsymbol{0}).$$

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_6''\equiv\begin{pmatrix}\boldsymbol{L}\ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z}\ \boldsymbol{V}_3\ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here we zeroed out everything except the main diagonal in V with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Proposition E.45.

6.3 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_6^3 \leftarrow \texttt{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_6'', 2z+1, 3z, f_6^3)$  where  $f_6^3$  is defined as:

BaseConv 
$$(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_{6}'', W_{6}, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}, \mathbf{1}^{4z \times z}).$$

Where  $W_6$  is defined as it was in math step 6.

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_6^3 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{L} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \ \boldsymbol{V}_4 \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here, because we can only repeat whole matrices and not each row, we are permuting the values on the main diagonal to reorganize them to be as if they were repeated each row at a time with  ${\tt BaseConv}(4z,O(1),z,4z,z)$  via Corollary F.46.

6.4 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_6^4 \leftarrow \texttt{remember}\,(\mathbf{Y}_6^3,2z,3z-1,f_6^4)$  where  $f_6^4$  is defined as:

$$\texttt{cumulative\_sum}\,(\overline{\overline{\mathbf{Y}}}_6^3)\,.$$

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_6^4 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} L \ \mathbf{0}^{z\times z} \ V_5 \ \mathbf{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here, we use cumulative\_sum so that the final row in the matrix stores each value in each column with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Corollary F.46.

6.5 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_6^5 \leftarrow \texttt{remember}\,(\mathbf{Y}_6^4,2z,3z-1,f_6^5)$  where  $f_6^5$  is defined as:

shift\_up 
$$(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_6^4, N\overline{b}-1)$$
 .

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_6^5 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{L} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \ \boldsymbol{V}_6 \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here, we shift this final row up to be in the first row with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Proposition F.38.

6.6 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_6 \leftarrow \texttt{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_6^5, 2z, 3z - 1, f_6^6)$  where  $f_6^6$  is defined as:

$$\texttt{cumulative\_sum}\,(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_6^5)\,.$$

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_6 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{L} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \ \boldsymbol{V}_1 \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z\times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here we copied the first row to each row in  ${\bf V}$  with  ${\tt BaseConv}(4z,O(1),z,4z,z)$  via Corollary F.46. This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y_6} \equiv \begin{pmatrix} L \ 0^{z \times z} \ \hline V_1 \ 0^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This step is computed with With BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Corollary F.46.

- 7. Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_7$  in steps 7.1-7.3.
  - 7.1 Compute  $\mathbf{Y}_7' \leftarrow \text{remember}(\mathbf{Y}_6, 1, z, f_7)$  where  $f_7$  is defined as:

repeat\_columns 
$$(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_6, \overline{b})$$
 .

This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y_7'} \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{L'} \ \boldsymbol{0^{z \times z}} \ \boldsymbol{V_1} \ \boldsymbol{0^{z \times z}} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here we repeat the columns of  $\boldsymbol{L}$  with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Corollary F.46.

7.2 We want to Hadamard the first and third position which we can do with:

$$\mathbf{Y}_7'' \equiv \text{BASECONV}(\mathbf{Y}_7', \mathbf{I}^{z \times z}, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}, \mathbf{h}^7, \mathbf{0}^{4z \times z}).$$

Where  $h^7 \in \mathbb{R}^{z \times z}$  is defined as:

$$\bm{h}^7 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \bm{0}^{z \times z} \ \bm{0}^z \ \bm{e}_1^z \ \bm{0}^z \end{pmatrix}.$$

Here we Hadamard the L and  $V_1$  together. Which results in:

$$\boldsymbol{Y_7''} = \begin{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \boldsymbol{0}^{z \times z} \ \hline \boldsymbol{U} \ \boldsymbol{0}^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}$$

This is done with with BaseConv(4z, 1, z, 4z, z) via a single BaseConv layer.

7.3 Finally, we shift-up(Y′′ 7 , 2z). This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y}_7 \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \bar{\bar{\mathbf{D}}^z} \ \mathbf{O}^z \ \mathbf{O}^z \end{pmatrix}$$

.

This is done with with BaseConv(4z, O(1), z, 4z, z) via Proposition [F.38.](#page-52-0)

- 8. Convert Y<sup>7</sup> to the final output.
  - 8.1 Here we will move everything to the first block using:

$$\mathbf{Y}_8' \equiv \texttt{sum\_column\_blocks}(\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_7, b).$$

$$\mathbf{Y_8'} \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \overline{L}_2 \ 0^{z \times z} \ \hline 0^{z \times z} \ 0^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}$$

.

This is done with with BaseConv(4z, 1, z, 4z, z) via Corollary [F.46.](#page-62-0)

8.2 Compute Y<sup>8</sup> ← remember(Y′ 8 , 1, z, f8) where f<sup>8</sup> is defined as:

one\_hot\_encoding(
$$\overline{\mathbf{Y}}_8'$$
).

This converts L to be 1-hot encoded in O(N log N) BaseConv layers. This results in:

$$\mathbf{Y_8} \equiv \begin{pmatrix} \overline{L}_1 \ \hline 0^{z \times z} \ \hline 0^{z \times z} \ \hline 0^{z \times z} \end{pmatrix}.$$

This is done with with BaseConv(4z, O(⌈log log N⌉), z, 4z, z) via Corollary [F.46.](#page-62-0)

Overall cost: We can solve the MQAR problem with BaseConv(4z, O(⌈log log N⌉) + O(1), z, 4z, z) by stacking the layers presented above.
